          <article class="post-5381 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-crafts tag-kid-friendly tag-nontoxic author-chrisy default" id="post-5381" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Article">
           <header>
            <h1 class="entry-title" itemprop="headline">
             Homemade Mod Podge
            </h1>
            <div class="entry-meta entry-meta-above">
             <span class="post-date updated" id="content_dateblock">
              <time class="entry-date published updated" datetime="2015-01-10T07:00:23+00:00" itemprop="datePublished">
               01/10/15
              </time>
              <div id="hiding">
               <time class="entry-time" datetime="2015-01-10T07:00:23+00:00">
                7:00 am
               </time>
              </div>

       <div class="desktopmobilefix mobilewidth block block-type-content block-fluid-height block-mirrored block-mirroring-bv95581c5617bb2a block-original-b7k55873c3951fe2" data-alias="desktop_content_post" id="block-bv95581c5617bb2a">
        <div class="block-content">
         <div class="loop">
          <article class="post-5381 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-crafts tag-kid-friendly tag-nontoxic author-chrisy default" id="post-5381" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Article">
           <header>
            <div class="entry-meta entry-meta-above">
             <span class="post-date updated" id="content_dateblock">
              <time class="entry-date published updated" datetime="2015-01-10T07:00:23+00:00" itemprop="datePublished">
               01/10/15
              </time>
             </span>
             <span id="content_filedunder">
              <a href="http://homemadehooplah.com/category/diy/crafts/" rel="category tag">
               Crafts
              </a>
             </span>
             <span id="content_comments">
              <a class="entry-comments" href="http://homemadehooplah.com/homemade-mod-podge/#comments" title="Homemade Mod Podge  Comments">
               0
               <i class="fa fa-comment">
               </i>
              </a>
             </span>
             <span class="vcard author post-author" id="hiding">
              <span class="fn">
               Chrisy
              </span>
             </span>
            </div>
            <!-- .entry-meta -->
           </header>
           <div class="entry-content" itemprop="text">
            <input class="jpibfi" type="hidden"/>
            <p>
             One of my new years resolutions for 2015 was to
             <em>
              finally
             </em>
             get back into doing more DIY projects. When I first started this blog I thought it would give me the motivation I needed to work through the (seemingly endless)list of projects I wanted to do, but instead I focused all my energy on learning to cook. And while thats not a bad thing by any means, it doesnt get me any closer gets me no closer to fixing up this house or filling all our blank walls. Actually, all this cooking Ive been doing has made an old problem worse  my cabinetsan absolute
             <em>
              wreck
             </em>
             from trying to hold all the cooking ingredients I now own. Boxes of Tuna Helper were so much easier to store.
            </p>
            <p>
             My cabinet woes brings me to my first DIY project since my self-imposed hiatus: making my own Homemade Mod Podge. On the surface thosetwo might not seem related, but I plan to use a lot of Mod Podge for the custom storageboxes Im creating to organize the terror that is my baking shelf. Ill be posting about how to make thoseas well as I get everything together.
            </p>
            <p>
             But for now, back to the Mod Podge. For those that dont know, Mod Podge is decoupage, and decoupage is used toadhere paper or fabric to just about any surface. In some cases its even used as a finish. In a nutshell, Mod Podge makes upcycling possible by allowing us to decorate and cover our crafts in the stylish designs wed prefer.
            </p>
            <p>
             There are a couple of homemade recipes for decoupageout there, but I opted to go with
             <a href="http://365daysofdiy.blogspot.ca/2012/01/homemade-modge-podge.html" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'http://365daysofdiy.blogspot.ca/2012/01/homemade-modge-podge.html', 'this one']);" target="_blank">
              this one
             </a>
             . I already had all of the ingredients
             <em>
              and
             </em>
             I liked the fact that it was completely nontoxic. This means that if my dogs somehow got their paws on the decoupage (or something Ive used the decoupage on) I dont need to worry about it making them sick. For the same reason, this homemade decoupage would be greatfor doing craft projects with kids.
            </p>
            <p>
             However, its important to note that the same person who published this homemade recipe also dida
             <a href="http://365daysofdiy.blogspot.com/2012/12/mod-podge-vs-homemade-decoupage.html" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'http://365daysofdiy.blogspot.com/2012/12/mod-podge-vs-homemade-decoupage.html', 'side-by-side comparison']);" target="_blank">
              side-by-side comparison
             </a>
             of the brand name Mod Podge, her recipe, and another DIY decoupage that is frequently on Pinterest. In her tests, the brand name Mod Podge still came out on top, but if youre interested in saving afew dollars (and like the idea of nontoxic) then this hommeade recipe shouldbe sufficient for most projects.
            </p>
            <h6>
             The Ingredients
            </h6>
            <ul>
             <li class="p1">
              1 and 1/2 cups all-purpose flour
             </li>
             <li class="p1">
              1/4 cup of granulated sugar
             </li>
             <li class="p1">
              1 tsp oil (any kind)
             </li>
             <li class="p1">
              1 and 1/4 cups water
             </li>
             <li class="p1">
              empty jar (with an air tight lid)
             </li>
            </ul>
            <h6>
             The Instructions
            </h6>
            <p>
             Measure out all of your ingredients and add them to a large saucepan. Turn the heat on low and slowly whisk them together, workingout all of the clumps in the flour.
            </p>
            <p>
             The trick is not to let the mixture boil. It just needs to be heated enough to dissolve the sugar.If the ingredients get too thick, add 1 tablespoon of water at a time until its the consistency youd like. If youd like a shinier finish, add a little more oil (1 tsp at a time, checking consistency).
            </p>
            <p>
             <a href="http://homemadehooplah.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/homemademodpodge2.jpg">
              <img alt="Homemade Mod Podge! Save a few bucks and make your own homemade mod podge with ingredients you already have. It's nontoxic and kid friendly! | HomemadeHooplah.com" class="aligncenter wp-image-5386 size-full" height="900" src="http://homemadehooplah.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/homemademodpodge2.jpg" width="600"/>
             </a>
            </p>
            <p>
             I cooked mine for a total of5minutes, stirring occassionally. When the texture was smooth, I poured it into a spare canning jar I had. The recipe makes about 2 cups of decoupage.
            </p>
            <p>
             <a href="http://homemadehooplah.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/homemademodpodge3.jpg">
              <img alt="Homemade Mod Podge! Save a few bucks and make your own homemade mod podge with ingredients you already have. It's nontoxic and kid friendly! | HomemadeHooplah.com" class="aligncenter wp-image-5387 size-full" height="900" src="http://homemadehooplah.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/homemademodpodge3.jpg" width="600"/>
             </a>
            </p>
            <h6>
             Storage &amp; Useage
            </h6>
            <p>
             Wait for the decoupage to cool down before using, and then store in a cool place without direct sunlight. The ingredients may separate inbetween uses  just give the bottle a good shake to combine them again.
            </p>
            <p>
             Try to use the mod podge within 1-2 days of making it, then throw out any thats left over. There areno preservatives in the ingredients, so sadly it wont last forever in liquid form. Thankfully its cheap to make!
            </p>
            <script type="text/javascript">

            </script>
